class="firstHeading" lang="en">Cricket</h1>\t\t\t<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">\n\t\t\t\t<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>\t\t\t\t<div search</a>\n\t\t\t\t<div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">This article is about the sport. For other uses, see <a href="/wiki/Cricketer_(disambiguation)" class="mw-disambig" title="Cricketer (disambiguation)">Cricketer (disambiguation)</a>.</div>\n<p class="mw-empty-elt">\n\n\n</p>\n<table class="infobox vcard" style="width:22em"><caption class="fn" style="padding-bottom:0.2em;">Cricket</caption><tbody><tr><td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">\n<a href="/wiki/File:Eden_Gardens_under_floodlights_during_a_match.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Eden Gardens under floodlights during a match.jpg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Eden_Gardens_under_floodlights_during_a_match.jpg/300px-Eden_Gardens_under_floodlights_during_a_match.jpg" width="300" height="200" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Eden_Gardens_under_floodlights_during_a_match.jpg/450px-Eden_Gardens_under_floodlights_during_a_match.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Eden_Gardens_under_floodlights_during_a_match.jpg/600px-Eden_Gardens_under_floodlights_during_a_match.jpg 2x" data-file-width="750" data-file-height="500" /></a><div><div style="padding:0.1em 0;line-height:1.2em;"><a href="/wiki/Eden_Gardens" title="Eden Gardens">Eden Gardens</a>, <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a> under floodlights during <a href="/wiki/2016_ICC_World_Twenty20_Final" title="2016 ICC World Twenty20 Final">2016 ICC World Twenty20 Final</a></div></div></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="padding-top:0.2em;line-height:1.2em; padding-right:1.0em;">Glossary</th><td style="line-height:1.3em;">\n<a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_cricket_terms" title="Glossary of cricket terms">Glossary of cricket terms</a></td></tr><tr><th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;background:#eee;">Presence</th></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="padding-top:0.2em;line-height:1.2em; padding-right:1.0em;">Country or&#160;region</th><td style="line-height:1.3em;">\nWorldwide but most prominent in the <a href="/wiki/Indian_Sub-Continent" class="mw-redirect" title="Indian Sub-Continent">Indian Sub-Continent</a>, <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">Australia</a>, <a href="/wiki/British_Isles" title="British Isles">British Isles</a>,  <a href="/wiki/Southern_Africa" title="Southern Africa">Southern Africa</a>, <a href="/wiki/West_Indies" title="West Indies">West Indies</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="padding-top:0.2em;line-height:1.2em; padding-right:1.0em;"><a href="/wiki/Olympic_Games" title="Olympic Games">Olympic</a></th><td style="line-height:1.3em;">\nno (<a href="/wiki/1900_Summer_Olympics" title="1900 Summer Olympics">1900 Summer Olympics</a> only)</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><b>Cricket</b> is a <a href="/wiki/Bat-and-ball_games" title="Bat-and-ball games">bat-and-ball game</a> played between two teams of eleven players. It is set on a <a href="/wiki/Cricket_field" title="Cricket field">cricket field</a> centred on a 20-metre (22-yard) <a href="/wiki/Cricket_pitch" title="Cricket pitch">pitch</a> with two <a href="/wiki/Wickets" class="mw-redirect" title="Wickets">wickets</a> each comprising a <a href="/wiki/Bail_(cricket)" title="Bail (cricket)">bail</a> balanced on three <a href="/wiki/Stump_(cricket)" title="Stump (cricket)">stumps</a>. For each phase of play, or <a href="/wiki/Innings" title="Innings">innings</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Batting_(cricket)" title="Batting (cricket)">batting</a> side tries to score as many <a href="/wiki/Run_(cricket)" title="Run (cricket)">runs</a> as possible after striking the <a href="/wiki/Cricket_ball" title="Cricket ball">cricket ball</a> thrown at the wicket (or <a href="/wiki/Delivery_(cricket)" title="Delivery (cricket)">delivery</a>) with the bat, while a <a href="/wiki/Bowling_(cricket)" title="Bowling (cricket)">bowling</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fielding_(cricket)" title="Fielding (cricket)">fielding</a> side tries to prevent this and <a href="/wiki/Dismissal_(cricket)" title="Dismissal (cricket)">dismiss</a> each player (so they are "out"). Means of dismissal can include being <a href="/wiki/Bowled" title="Bowled">bowled</a>, when the ball directly hits the stumps and dislodges the bails, and by the fielding side catching the ball after it is hit by the bat, but before it hits the ground. When ten players have been dismissed, the innings end and the teams swap roles. The side with the most runs generally wins, though there are exceptions where the game is drawn instead. The game is adjudicated by two <a href="/wiki/Umpire_(cricket)" title="Umpire (cricket)">umpires</a>, aided by a <a href="/wiki/Third_umpire" title="Third umpire">third umpire</a> and <a href="/wiki/Match_referee" title="Match referee">match referee</a> in international matches. They communicate with two off-field <a href="/wiki/Scoring_(cricket)" title="Scoring (cricket)">scorers</a> (one per team) who record all the match\'s <a href="/wiki/Cricket_statistics" title="Cricket statistics">statistical information</a>.\n</p><p>There are various <a href="/wiki/Forms_of_cricket" title="Forms of cricket">formats</a> ranging from <a href="/wiki/Twenty20" title="Twenty20">Twenty20</a>, played over a few hours with each team batting for a single <a href="/wiki/Innings" title="Innings">innings</a> of 20 <a href="/wiki/Over_(cricket)" title="Over (cricket)">overs</a> (i.e. 120 deliveries), to <a href="/wiki/Test_cricket" title="Test cricket">Test matches</a>, played over five days with unlimited overs and the teams each batting for two innings of unlimited length. Traditionally cricketers play in all-white <a href="/wiki/Cricket_clothing_and_equipment" title="Cricket clothing and equipment">kit</a>, but in <a href="/wiki/Limited_overs_cricket" title="Limited overs cricket">limited overs cricket</a> they wear club or team colours. In addition to the basic kit, some players wear <a href="/wiki/Cricket_clothing_and_equipment" title="Cricket clothing and equipment">protective gear</a> to prevent injury caused by the ball, which is a hard, solid spheroid made of compressed <a href="/wiki/Leather" title="Leather">leather</a> with a slightly raised sewn seam enclosing a <a href="/wiki/Cork_(material)" title="Cork (material)">cork</a> core which is layered with tightly wound string.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/History_of_cricket" title="History of cricket">Historically</a>, cricket\'s origins are uncertain and the earliest definite reference is in south-east England in the middle of the 16th century. It spread globally with the expansion of the <a href="/wiki/British_Empire" title="British Empire">British Empire</a>, leading to the first international matches in the second half of the 19th century. The game\'s governing body is the <a href="/wiki/International_Cricket_Council" title="International Cricket Council">International Cricket Council</a> (ICC), which has over 100 members, twelve of which are <a href="/wiki/List_of_International_Cricket_Council_members" title="List of International Cricket Council members">full members</a> who play Test matches. The game\'s rules are held in a code called the <i><a href="/wiki/Laws_of_Cricket" title="Laws of Cricket">Laws of Cricket</a></i> which is owned and maintained by <a href="/wiki/Marylebone_Cricket_Club" title="Marylebone Cricket Club">Marylebone Cricket Club</a> (MCC) in London. The sport is followed primarily in the <a href="/wiki/Indian_subcontinent" title="Indian subcontinent">Indian subcontinent</a>, <a href="/wiki/Australasia" title="Australasia">Australasia</a>, the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ireland" title="Ireland">Ireland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Southern_Africa" title="Southern Africa">southern Africa</a> and the <a href="/wiki/West_Indies" title="West Indies">West Indies</a>, its globalisation occurring during the expansion of the British Empire and remaining popular into the 21st century.<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Women%27s_cricket" title="Women&#39;s cricket">Women\'s cricket</a>, which is organised and played separately, has also achieved international standard. The most successful side playing <a href="/wiki/International_cricket" title="International cricket">international cricket</a> is <a href="/wiki/Australia_national_cricket_team" title="Australia national cricket team">Australia</a>, having won seven <a href="/wiki/One_Day_International" title="One Day International">One Day International</a> trophies, including five <a href="/wiki/Cricket_World_Cup" title="Cricket World Cup">World Cups</a>, more than any other country, and having been the <a href="/wiki/ICC_Test_Championship" title="ICC Test Championship">top-rated Test side</a> more than any other country.\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div tocsection-22"><a href="#Women&#39;s_cricket"><span class="tocnumber">3</span> <span class="toctext">Women\'s cricket</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-23"><a href="#Governance"><span class="tocnumber">4</span> <span class="toctext">Governance</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-24"><a href="#Types_of_match"><span class="tocnumber">5</span> <span class="toctext">Types of match</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-25"><a href="#International_competitions"><span class="tocnumber">6</span> <span class="toctext">International competitions</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-26"><a href="#National_competitions"><span class="tocnumber">7</span> <span class="toctext">National competitions</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-27"><a href="#First-class"><span class="tocnumber">7.1</span> <span class="toctext">First-class</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-28"><a href="#Limited_overs"><span class="tocnumber">7.2</span> <span class="toctext">Limited overs</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-29"><a href="#Other"><span class="tocnumber">7.3</span> <span class="toctext">Other</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-30"><a href="#Club_and_school_cricket"><span class="tocnumber">8</span> <span class="toctext">Club and school cricket</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-31"><a href="#Culture"><span class="tocnumber">9</span> <span class="toctext">Culture</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-32"><a href="#Influence_on_everyday_life"><span class="tocnumber">9.1</span> <span class="toctext">Influence on everyday life</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-33"><a href="#In_the_arts_and_popular_culture"><span class="tocnumber">9.2</span> <span class="toctext">In the arts and popular culture</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-34"><a href="#Influence_on_other_sports"><span class="tocnumber">9.3</span> <span class="toctext">Influence on other sports</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-35"><a href="#See_also"><span class="tocnumber">10</span> <span class="toctext">See also</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-36"><a href="#Footnotes"><span class="tocnumber">11</span> <span class="toctext">Footnotes</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-37"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">12</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-38"><a href="#Sources"><span class="tocnumber">13</span> <span class="toctext">Sources</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-39"><a href="#Further_reading"><span class="tocnumber">14</span> <span class="toctext">Further reading</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-40"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">15</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_cricket" title="History of cricket">History of cricket</a></div>\n<table class="vertical-navbox nowraplinks plainlist" style="float:right;clear:right;width:22.0em;margin:0 0 1.0em 1.0em;background:#f9f9f9;border:1px solid #aaa;padding:0.2em;border-spacing:0.4em 0;text-align:center;line-height:1.4em;font-size:88%"><tbody><tr><td style="padding-top:0.4em;line-height:1.2em">Part of <a href="/wiki/Category:Cricket" title="Category:Cricket">a series</a> on</td></tr><tr><th style="padding:0.2em 0.4em 0.2em;padding-top:0;font-size:145%;line-height:1.2em;font-size:175%;padding:0 0.2em 0.4em;"><a class="mw-selflink selflink">Cricket</a></th></tr><tr><td style="padding:0.2em 0 0.4em;padding:0 0 1.0em;"><div class="center"><div class="floatnone"><a href="/wiki/File:Cricket_-_The_Noun_Project.svg" class="image" title="Cricket pictogram"><img alt="Cricket pictogram" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Cricket_-_The_Noun_Project.svg/45px-Cricket_-_The_Noun_Project.svg.png" width="45" height="45" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Cricket_-_The_Noun_Project.svg/68px-Cricket_-_The_Noun_Project.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Cricket_-_The_Noun_Project.svg/90px-Cricket_-_The_Noun_Project.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="512" /></a></div></div></td></tr><tr><td style="padding:0 0.1em 0.4em">\n<div class="NavFrame" style="border:none;padding:0"><div class="NavHead" style="font-size:105%;background:transparent;text-align:left;border-bottom:1px solid #cee0f2;background:none;text-align:center;"><a href="/wiki/Forms_of_cricket" title="Forms of cricket">Forms of cricket</a></div><div class="NavContent hlist" style="font-size:105%;padding:0.2em 0 0.4em;text-align:center">\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Test_cricket" title="Test cricket">Test cricket</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/One_Day_International" title="One Day International">One Day International</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Twenty20_International" title="Twenty20 International">Twenty20 International</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/First-class_cricket" title="First-class cricket">First-class cricket</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Limited_overs_cricket" title="Limited overs cricket">Limited overs cricket</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/List_A_cricket" title="List A cricket">List A cricket</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Twenty20" title="Twenty20">Twenty20</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/100-ball_cricket" title="100-ball cricket">100-ball cricket</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Club_cricket" title="Club cricket">Club cricket</a></li></ul></div></div></td>\n</tr><tr><td style="padding:0 0.1em 0.4em">\n<div class="NavFrame" style="border:none;padding:0"><div class="NavHead" style="font-size:105%;background:transparent;text-align:left;border-bottom:1px solid #cee0f2;background:none;text-align:center;"><a href="/wiki/History_of_cricket" title="History of cricket">History of cricket</a></div><div class="NavContent hlist" style="font-size:105%;padding:0.2em 0 0.4em;text-align:center">\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/History_of_cricket_to_1725" title="History of cricket to 1725">History of cricket to 1725</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/History_of_cricket_(1726%E2%80%931763)" title="History of cricket (1726\xe2\x80\x931763)">History of cricket (1726\xe2\x80\x931763)</a></li></ul></div></div></td>\n</tr><tr><td style="text-align:right;font-size:115%;padding-top: 0.6em;"><div class="plainlinks hlist navbar mini"><ul><li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:Cricket_sidebar" title="Template:Cricket sidebar"><abbr title="View this template">v</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-talk"><a href="/wiki/Template_talk:Cricket_sidebar" title="Template talk:Cricket sidebar"><abbr title="Discuss this template">t</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-edit"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:Cricket_sidebar&amp;action=edit"><abbr title="Edit this template">e</abbr></a></li></ul></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Origins">Origins</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_cricket_to_1725" title="History of cricket to 1725">History of cricket to 1725</a></div>\n<p>Cricket is one of many games in the "club ball" sphere that basically involve hitting a ball with a hand-held implement; others are <a href="/wiki/Baseball" title="Baseball">baseball</a>, <a href="/wiki/Golf" title="Golf">golf</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hockey" title="Hockey">hockey</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tennis" title="Tennis">tennis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Squash_(sport)" title="Squash (sport)">squash</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Table_tennis" title="Table tennis">table tennis</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-JM17_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JM17-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> In cricket\'s case, a key difference is the existence of a solid target structure, the wicket (originally, it is thought, a "wicket gate" through which sheep were herded), that the batsman must defend.<sup id="cite_ref-BWC1_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BWC1-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> The cricket historian <a href="/wiki/Harry_Altham" title="Harry Altham">Harry Altham</a> identified three "groups" of "club ball" games: the "hockey group", in which the ball is driven to and fro between two targets (the goals); the "golf group", in which the ball is driven towards an undefended target (the hole); and the "cricket group", in which "the ball is aimed at a mark (the wicket) and driven away from it".<sup id="cite_ref-HSA19_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HSA19-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>It is generally believed that cricket originated as a children\'s game in the south-eastern counties of England, sometime during the <a href="/wiki/England_in_the_Middle_Ages" title="England in the Middle Ages">medieval period</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-BWC1_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BWC1-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> Although there are claims for prior dates, the earliest definite reference to cricket being played comes from evidence given at a court case in <a href="/wiki/Guildford" title="Guildford">Guildford</a> on Monday, 17 January 1597 (<a href="/wiki/Julian_calendar" title="Julian calendar">Julian calendar</a>; equating to 30 January 1598 in the <a href="/wiki/Gregorian_calendar" title="Gregorian calendar">Gregorian calendar</a>). The case concerned ownership of a certain plot of land and the court heard the testimony of a 59-year-old <a href="/wiki/Coroner" title="Coroner">coroner</a>, <a href="/wiki/John_Derrick" title="John Derrick">John Derrick</a>, who gave witness that:<sup id="cite_ref-HSA21_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HSA21-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-DU3_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DU3-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-JM19_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JM19-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<blockquote><p>"Being a scholler in the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Grammar_School,_Guildford" title="Royal Grammar School, Guildford">ffree schoole of Guldeford</a> hee and diverse of his fellows did runne and play there at creckett and other plaies".</p></blockquote>\n<p>Given Derrick\'s age, it was about half a century earlier when he was at school and so it is certain that cricket was being played c. 1550 by boys in <a href="/wiki/Surrey" title="Surrey">Surrey</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-JM19_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JM19-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> The view that it was originally a children\'s game is reinforced by <a href="/wiki/Randle_Cotgrave" title="Randle Cotgrave">Randle Cotgrave</a>\'s 1611 English-French dictionary in which he defined the noun "<i>crosse</i>" as "the crooked staff wherewith boys play at cricket" and the verb form "<i>crosser</i>" as "to play at cricket".<sup id="cite_ref-HSA22_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HSA22-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-JM31_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JM31-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>One possible source for the sport\'s name is the <a href="/wiki/Old_English_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Old English language">Old English</a> word "<i>cryce</i>" (or "<i>cricc</i>") meaning a crutch or staff. In <a href="/wiki/Samuel_Johnson" title="Samuel Johnson">Samuel Johnson</a>\'s <i>Dictionary</i>, he derived cricket from "<i>cryce</i>, Saxon, a stick".<sup id="cite_ref-HSA21_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HSA21-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> In <a href="/wiki/Old_French" title="Old French">Old French</a>, the word "<i>criquet</i>" seems to have meant a kind of club or stick.<sup id="cite_ref-DB3_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DB3-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> Given the strong medieval trade connections between south-east England and the <a href="/wiki/County_of_Flanders" title="County of Flanders">County of Flanders</a> when the latter belonged to the <a href="/wiki/Duchy_of_Burgundy" title="Duchy of Burgundy">Duchy of Burgundy</a>, the name may have been derived from the <a href="/wiki/Middle_Dutch" title="Middle Dutch">Middle Dutch</a> (in use in <a href="/wiki/County_of_Flanders" title="County of Flanders">Flanders</a> at the time) "<i>krick</i>"(<i>-e</i>), meaning a stick (crook).<sup id="cite_ref-DB3_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DB3-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> Another possible source is the Middle Dutch word "<i>krickstoel</i>", meaning a long low stool used for kneeling in church and which resembled the long low <a href="/wiki/Wicket" title="Wicket">wicket</a> with two <a href="/wiki/Stump_(cricket)" title="Stump (cricket)">stumps</a> used in early cricket.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> According to Heiner Gillmeister, a European language expert of <a href="/wiki/Bonn_University" class="mw-redirect" title="Bonn University">Bonn University</a>, "cricket" derives from the Middle Dutch phrase for <a href="/wiki/Hockey" title="Hockey">hockey</a>, <i>met de (krik ket)sen</i> (i.e., "with the stick chase").<sup id="cite_ref-17CGC_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17CGC-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> Gillmeister has suggested that not only the name but also the sport itself may be of Flemish origin.<sup id="cite_ref-17CGC_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17CGC-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Growth_of_amateur_and_professional_cricket_in_England">Growth of amateur and professional cricket in England</span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Historical_cricket_bat_art.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Historical_cricket_bat_art.jpg/220px-Historical_cricket_bat_art.jpg" width="220" height="199" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Historical_cricket_bat_art.jpg/330px-Historical_cricket_bat_art.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Historical_cricket_bat_art.jpg/440px-Historical_cricket_bat_art.jpg 2x" data-file-width="956" data-file-height="866" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Historical_cricket_bat_art.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Evolution of the cricket bat. The original "hockey stick" (left) evolved into the straight bat from c. 1760 when <a href="/wiki/Pitched_delivery_bowling" title="Pitched delivery bowling">pitched delivery bowling</a> began.</div></div></div>\n<p>Although the main object of the game has always been to score the most <a href="/wiki/Run_(cricket)" title="Run (cricket)">runs</a>, the early form of cricket differed from the modern game in certain key technical aspects. The <a href="/wiki/Cricket_ball" title="Cricket ball">ball</a> was <a href="/wiki/Underarm_bowling" title="Underarm bowling">bowled underarm</a> by the <a href="/wiki/Bowling_(cricket)" title="Bowling (cricket)">bowler</a> and all along the ground towards a <a href="/wiki/Batting_(cricket)" title="Batting (cricket)">batsman</a> armed with a <a href="/wiki/Cricket_bat" title="Cricket bat">bat</a> that, in shape, resembled a <a href="/wiki/Hockey_stick" title="Hockey stick">hockey stick</a>; the batsman defended a low, two-stump <a href="/wiki/Wicket" title="Wicket">wicket</a>; and runs were called "notches" because the <a href="/wiki/Scoring_(cricket)" title="Scoring (cricket)">scorers</a> recorded them by notching tally sticks.<sup id="cite_ref-DB9_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DB9-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-BWC2_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BWC2-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-JM21_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JM21-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1611, the year Cotgrave\'s dictionary was published, <a href="/wiki/Ecclesiastical_court" title="Ecclesiastical court">ecclesiastical court</a> records at <a href="/wiki/Sidlesham" title="Sidlesham">Sidlesham</a> in <a href="/wiki/Sussex" title="Sussex">Sussex</a> state that two parishioners, Bartholomew Wyatt and Richard Latter, failed to attend church on Easter Sunday because they were playing cricket. They were fined 12<a href="/wiki/Penny_(British_pre-decimal_coin)" title="Penny (British pre-decimal coin)">d</a> each and ordered to do <a href="/wiki/Penance" title="Penance">penance</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> This is the earliest mention of adult participation in cricket and it was around the same time that the earliest known organised inter-parish or <a href="/wiki/Village_cricket" title="Village cricket">village</a> match was played \xe2\x80\x93 at <a href="/wiki/Chevening,_Kent" title="Chevening, Kent">Chevening, Kent</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-HSA21_5-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HSA21-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-DU4_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DU4-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> In 1624, a player called <a href="/wiki/Jasper_Vinall" title="Jasper Vinall">Jasper Vinall</a> died after he was accidentally struck on the head during a match between two parish teams in Sussex.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Cricket remained a low-key local pursuit for much of the century.<sup id="cite_ref-JM31_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JM31-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> It is known, through numerous references found in the records of ecclesiastical court cases, to have been proscribed at times by the <a href="/wiki/Puritans" title="Puritans">Puritans</a> before and during the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_England" title="Commonwealth of England">Commonwealth</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-DU11_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DU11-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> The problem was nearly always the issue of Sunday play as the Puritans considered cricket to be "profane" if played on the <a href="/wiki/Sabbath" title="Sabbath">Sabbath</a>, especially if large crowds and/or <a href="/wiki/Gambling" title="Gambling">gambling</a> were involved.<sup id="cite_ref-DB7_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DB7-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-JM23_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JM23-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>According to the social historian <a href="/wiki/Derek_Birley" title="Derek Birley">Derek Birley</a>, there was a "great upsurge of sport after the <a href="/wiki/English_Restoration" class="mw-redirect" title="English Restoration">Restoration</a>" in 1660.<sup id="cite_ref-DB11_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DB11-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> Gambling on sport became a problem significant enough for Parliament to pass the 1664 Gambling Act, limiting stakes to \xc2\xa3100 which was in any case a colossal sum exceeding the annual income of 99% of the population.<sup id="cite_ref-DB11_23-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DB11-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> Along with <a href="/wiki/Prizefighting" class="mw-redirect" title="Prizefighting">prizefighting</a>, <a href="/wiki/Horse_racing" title="Horse racing">horse racing</a> and blood sports, cricket was perceived to be a gambling sport.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> Rich patrons made matches for high stakes, forming teams in which they engaged the first professional players.<sup id="cite_ref-RW10_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RW10-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> By the end of the century, cricket had developed into a major sport which was spreading throughout England and was already being taken abroad by English mariners and colonisers \xe2\x80\x93 the earliest reference to cricket overseas is dated 1676.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> A 1697 newspaper report survives of "a great cricket match" played in Sussex "for fifty guineas apiece" \xe2\x80\x93 this is the earliest known reference to an <a href="/wiki/First-class_cricket#Important_matches_classification" title="First-class cricket">important match</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The patrons, and other players from the social class known as the "<a href="/wiki/Gentry" title="Gentry">gentry</a>", began to classify themselves as "<a href="/wiki/Amateur_status_in_first-class_cricket" title="Amateur status in first-class cricket">amateurs</a>"<sup id="cite_ref-amateur_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-amateur-28">&#91;fn 1&#93;</a></sup> to establish a clear distinction <i>vis-\xc3\xa0-vis</i> the professionals, who were invariably members of the <a href="/wiki/Working_class" title="Working class">working class</a>, even to the point of having separate changing and dining facilities.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> The gentry, including such high-ranking nobles as the <a href="/wiki/Duke_of_Richmond" title="Duke of Richmond">Dukes of Richmond</a>, exerted their honour code of <i><a href="/wiki/Noblesse_oblige" title="Noblesse oblige">noblesse oblige</a></i> to claim rights of leadership in any sporting contests they took part in, especially as it was necessary for them to play alongside their "social inferiors" if they were to win their bets.<sup id="cite_ref-DB19_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DB19-30">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> In time, a perception took hold that the typical amateur who played in <a href="/wiki/First-class_cricket" title="First-class cricket">first-class cricket</a>, until 1962 when amateurism was abolished, was someone with a <a href="/wiki/Public_school_(United_Kingdom)" title="Public school (United Kingdom)">public school</a> education who had then gone to one of <a href="/wiki/University_of_Cambridge" title="University of Cambridge">Cambridge</a> or <a href="/wiki/University_of_Oxford" title="University of Oxford">Oxford University</a> \xe2\x80\x93 society insisted that such people were "officers and gentlemen" whose destiny was to provide leadership.<sup id="cite_ref-CW23_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CW23-31">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> In a purely financial sense, the cricketing amateur would <i>theoretically</i> claim expenses for playing while his professional counterpart played under contract and was paid a wage or match fee; in practice, many amateurs claimed somewhat more than actual expenditure and the derisive term "shamateur" was coined to describe the syndrome.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-DB146_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DB146-33">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="English_cricket_in_the_18th_and_19th_centuries">English cricket in the 18th and 19th centuries</span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Francis_Cotes_-_The_young_cricketer_(1768).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Francis_Cotes_-_The_young_cricketer_%281768%29.jpg/170px-Francis_Cotes_-_The_young_cricketer_%281768%29.jpg" width="170" height="261" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Francis_Cotes_-_The_young_cricketer_%281768%29.jpg/255px-Francis_Cotes_-_The_young_cricketer_%281768%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Francis_Cotes_-_The_young_cricketer_%281768%29.jpg/340px-Francis_Cotes_-_The_young_cricketer_%281768%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3060" data-file-height="4690" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Francis_Cotes_-_The_young_cricketer_(1768).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Francis_Cotes" title="Francis Cotes">Francis Cotes</a>, <i>The Young Cricketer</i>, 1768</div></div></div>\n<p>The game underwent major development in the 18th century to become England\'s national sport.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Its success was underwritten by the twin necessities of patronage and betting.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> Cricket was prominent in London as early as 1707 and, in the middle years of the century, large crowds flocked to matches on the <a href="/wiki/Artillery_Ground" title="Artillery Ground">Artillery Ground</a> in Finsbury.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> The <a href="/wiki/Single_wicket_cricket" title="Single wicket cricket">single wicket</a> form of the sport attracted huge crowds and wagers to match, its popularity peaking in the <a href="/wiki/1748_English_cricket_season" title="1748 English cricket season">1748 season</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ASW_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ASW-35">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> Bowling underwent an evolution around 1760 when bowlers began to <a href="/wiki/Pitched_delivery_bowling" title="Pitched delivery bowling">pitch the ball</a> instead of rolling or skimming it towards the batsman. This caused a revolution in bat design because, to deal with the <a href="/wiki/Bouncing_ball" title="Bouncing ball">bouncing ball</a>, it was necessary to introduce the modern straight bat in place of the old "hockey stick" shape.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Hambledon_Club" title="Hambledon Club">Hambledon Club</a> was founded in the 1760s and, for the next twenty years until the formation of <a href="/wiki/Marylebone_Cricket_Club" title="Marylebone Cricket Club">Marylebone Cricket Club</a> (MCC) and the opening of <a href="/wiki/Lord%27s_Old_Ground" title="Lord&#39;s Old Ground">Lord\'s Old Ground</a> in 1787, Hambledon was both the game\'s greatest club and its focal point.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> MCC quickly became the sport\'s premier club and the custodian of the <i><a href="/wiki/Laws_of_Cricket" title="Laws of Cricket">Laws of Cricket</a></i>. New Laws introduced in the latter part of the 18th century included the three stump wicket and <a href="/wiki/Leg_before_wicket" title="Leg before wicket">leg before wicket</a> (lbw).<sup id="cite_ref-WCA63_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WCA63-37">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The 19th century saw <a href="/wiki/Underarm_bowling" title="Underarm bowling">underarm bowling</a> superseded by first <a href="/wiki/Roundarm_bowling" title="Roundarm bowling">roundarm</a> and then <a href="/wiki/Overarm_bowling" title="Overarm bowling">overarm bowling</a>. Both developments were controversial.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> Organisation of the game at county level led to the creation of the county clubs, starting with <a href="/wiki/Sussex_County_Cricket_Club" title="Sussex County Cricket Club">Sussex</a> in 1839.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> In December 1889, the eight leading county clubs formed the official <a href="/wiki/County_Championship" title="County Championship">County Championship</a>, which began in 1890.<sup id="cite_ref-AMCS_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AMCS-40">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The most famous player of the 19th century was <a href="/wiki/W._G._Grace" title="W. G. Grace">W. G. Grace</a>, who started his long and influential career in 1865. It was especially during the career of Grace that the distinction between amateurs and professionals became blurred by the existence of players like him who were nominally amateur but, in terms of their financial gain, <i>de facto</i> professional. Grace himself was said to have been paid more money for playing cricket than any professional.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p><p>The last two decades before the <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">First World War</a> have been called the "<a href="/wiki/Golden_Age_of_cricket" title="Golden Age of cricket">Golden Age of cricket</a>". It is a nostalgic name prompted by the collective sense of loss resulting from the war, but the period did produce some great players and memorable matches, especially as organised competition at county and Test level developed.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cricket_becomes_an_international_sport">Cricket becomes an international sport</span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:England_in_North_America_1859.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/England_in_North_America_1859.jpg/220px-England_in_North_America_1859.jpg" width="220" height="151" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/England_in_North_America_1859.jpg/330px-England_in_North_America_1859.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/England_in_North_America_1859.jpg/440px-England_in_North_America_1859.jpg 2x" data-file-width="937" data-file-height="643" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:England_in_North_America_1859.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The first English team to tour overseas, on board ship to North America, 1859</div></div></div>\n<p>Meanwhile, the British Empire had been instrumental in spreading the game overseas and by the middle of the 19th century it had become well established in Australia, the Caribbean, India, New Zealand, North America and South Africa.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> In 1844, the <a href="/wiki/United_States_v_Canada_(1844)" class="mw-redirect" title="United States v Canada (1844)">first-ever international match</a> took place between the <a href="/wiki/United_States_national_cricket_team" title="United States national cricket team">United States</a> and <a href="/wiki/Canada_national_cricket_team" title="Canada national cricket team">Canada</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> In 1859, a team of English players went to North America on <a href="/wiki/English_cricket_team_in_North_America_in_1859" title="English cricket team in North America in 1859">the first overseas tour</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The first Australian team to travel overseas consisted of <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_Australians" title="Indigenous Australians">Aboriginal</a> <a href="/wiki/Stockman_(Australia)" title="Stockman (Australia)">stockmen</a> who <a href="/wiki/Australian_Aboriginal_cricket_team_in_England_in_1868" title="Australian Aboriginal cricket team in England in 1868">toured England in 1868</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> In 1862, an English team made the first tour of Australia.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1876\xe2\x80\x9377, an <a href="/wiki/England_cricket_team" title="England cricket team">England team</a> took part in what was retrospectively recognised as the first-ever <a href="/wiki/Test_cricket" title="Test cricket">Test match</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Melbourne_Cricket_Ground" title="Melbourne Cricket Ground">Melbourne Cricket Ground</a> against <a href="/wiki/Australia_national_cricket_team" title="Australia national cricket team">Australia</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> The rivalry between England and Australia gave birth to <a href="/wiki/The_Ashes" title="The Ashes">The Ashes</a> in 1882 and this has remained Test cricket\'s most famous contest.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> Test cricket began to expand in 1888\xe2\x80\x9389 when <a href="/wiki/South_Africa_national_cricket_team" title="South Africa national cricket team">South Africa</a> played England.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="World_cricket_in_the_20th_century">World cricket in the 20th century</span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bradman%26Bat.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Bradman%26Bat.jpg/170px-Bradman%26Bat.jpg" width="170" height="222" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Bradman%26Bat.jpg/255px-Bradman%26Bat.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Bradman%26Bat.jpg/340px-Bradman%26Bat.jpg 2x" data-file-width="615" data-file-height="802" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bradman%26Bat.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Don_Bradman" title="Don Bradman">Don Bradman</a> of <a href="/wiki/Australia_national_cricket_team" title="Australia national cricket team">Australia</a> had a record Test batting average of 99.94.</div></div></div>\n<p>The inter-war years were dominated by Australia\'s <a href="/wiki/Don_Bradman" title="Don Bradman">Don Bradman</a>, statistically the greatest Test batsman of all time. Test cricket continued to expand during the 20th century with the addition of the <a href="/wiki/West_Indies_cricket_team" title="West Indies cricket team">West Indies</a> (1928), <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand_national_cricket_team" title="New Zealand national cricket team">New Zealand</a> (1930) and <a href="/wiki/India_national_cricket_team" title="India national cricket team">India</a> (1932) before the Second World War and then <a href="/wiki/Pakistan_national_cricket_team" title="Pakistan national cricket team">Pakistan</a> (1952), <a href="/wiki/Sri_Lanka_national_cricket_team" title="Sri Lanka national cricket team">Sri Lanka</a> (1982), <a href="/wiki/Zimbabwe_national_cricket_team" title="Zimbabwe national cricket team">Zimbabwe</a> (1992) and <a href="/wiki/Bangladesh_national_cricket_team" title="Bangladesh national cricket team">Bangladesh</a> (2000) in the post-war period.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> South Africa was banned from international cricket from 1970 to 1992 as part of the <a href="/wiki/Sporting_boycott_of_South_Africa_during_the_apartheid_era" title="Sporting boycott of South Africa during the apartheid era">apartheid boycott</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_rise_of_limited_overs_cricket">The rise of limited overs cricket</span></h3>\n<p>Cricket entered a new era in 1963 when English counties introduced the <a href="/wiki/Limited_overs_cricket" title="Limited overs cricket">limited overs</a> variant.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> As it was sure to produce a result, limited overs cricket was lucrative and the number of matches increased.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> The first <a href="/wiki/Limited_Overs_International" class="mw-redirect" title="Limited Overs International">Limited Overs International</a> was played in 1971 and the governing <a href="/wiki/International_Cricket_Council" title="International Cricket Council">International Cricket Council</a> (ICC), seeing its potential, staged the first limited overs <a href="/wiki/Cricket_World_Cup" title="Cricket World Cup">Cricket World Cup</a> in 1975.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> In the 21st century, a new limited overs form, <a href="/wiki/Twenty20" title="Twenty20">Twenty20</a>, made an immediate impact.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> On 22 June 2017, <a href="/wiki/Afghanistan_national_cricket_team" title="Afghanistan national cricket team">Afghanistan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ireland_cricket_team" title="Ireland cricket team">Ireland</a> became the 11th and 12th ICC full members, enabling them to play Test cricket.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Laws_and_gameplay">Laws and gameplay</span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Laws_of_Cricket" title="Laws of Cricket">Laws of Cricket</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Cricket_field_parts.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Cricket_field_parts.svg/200px-Cricket_field_parts.svg.png" width="200" height="220" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Cricket_field_parts.svg/300px-Cricket_field_parts.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Cricket_field_parts.svg/400px-Cricket_field_parts.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="2000" data-file-height="2200" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Cricket_field_parts.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A typical <a href="/wiki/Cricket_field" title="Cricket field">cricket field</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>In cricket, the rules of the game are specified in a code called <i><a href="/wiki/The_Laws_of_Cricket" class="mw-redirect" title="The Laws of Cricket">The Laws of Cricket</a></i> (hereinafter called "the Laws") which has a global remit. There are 42 Laws (always written with a capital "L"). The earliest known version of the code was drafted in 1744 and, since 1788, it has been owned and maintained by its custodian, the <a href="/wiki/Marylebone_Cricket_Club" title="Marylebone Cricket Club">Marylebone Cricket Club</a> (MCC) in London.<sup id="cite_ref-Laws_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Laws-56">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Playing_area">Playing area</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Cricket_field" title="Cricket field">Cricket field</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cricket_pitch" title="Cricket pitch">Cricket pitch</a>, <a href="/wiki/Crease_(cricket)" title="Crease (cricket)">Crease (cricket)</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Wicket" title="Wicket">Wicket</a></div>\n<p>Cricket is a <a href="/wiki/Bat-and-ball_games" title="Bat-and-ball games">bat-and-ball game</a> played on a <a href="/wiki/Cricket_field" title="Cricket field">cricket field</a> (see image, right) between two teams of eleven players each.<sup id="cite_ref-Law1_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Law1-57">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> The field is usually circular or oval in shape and the edge of the playing area is marked by a <a href="/wiki/Boundary_(cricket)" title="Boundary (cricket)">boundary</a>, which may be a fence, part of the stands, a rope, a painted line or a combination of these; the boundary must if possible be marked along its entire length.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In the approximate centre of the field is a rectangular <a href="/wiki/Cricket_pitch" title="Cricket pitch">pitch</a> (see image, below) on which a wooden target called a <a href="/wiki/Wicket" title="Wicket">wicket</a> is sited at each end; the wickets are placed 22 yards (20&#160;m) apart.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> The pitch is a flat surface 3 metres (9.8&#160;ft) wide, with very short grass that tends to be worn away as the game progresses (cricket can also be played on artificial surfaces, notably matting). Each wicket is made of three wooden <a href="/wiki/Stump_(cricket)" title="Stump (cricket)">stumps</a> topped by two <a href="/wiki/Bail_(cricket)" title="Bail (cricket)">bails</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:752px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Cricket_pitch.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Cricket_pitch.svg/750px-Cricket_pitch.svg.png" width="750" height="234" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Cricket_pitch.svg/1125px-Cricket_pitch.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Cricket_pitch.svg/1500px-Cricket_pitch.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="3200" data-file-height="1000" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Cricket_pitch.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Cricket pitch and creases</div></div></div></div>\n<p>As illustrated above, the pitch is marked at each end with four white painted lines: a <a href="/wiki/Crease_(cricket)" title="Crease (cricket)">bowling crease</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Crease_(cricket)" title="Crease (cricket)">popping crease</a> and two <a href="/wiki/Crease_(cricket)" title="Crease (cricket)">return creases</a>. The three stumps are aligned centrally on the bowling crease, which is eight feet eight inches long. The popping crease is drawn four feet in front of the bowling crease and parallel to it; although it is drawn as a twelve-foot line (six feet either side of the wicket), it is in fact unlimited in length. The return creases are drawn at right angles to the popping crease so that they intersect the ends of the bowling crease; each return crease is drawn as an eight-foot line, so that it extends four feet behind the bowling crease, but is also in fact unlimited in length.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Match_structure_and_closure">Match structure and closure</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Innings" title="Innings">Innings</a> and <a href="/wiki/Result_(cricket)" title="Result (cricket)">Result (cricket)</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:A_modern_Cricket_bat_(back_view).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/A_modern_Cricket_bat_%28back_view%29.jpg/170px-A_modern_Cricket_bat_%28back_view%29.jpg" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/A_modern_Cricket_bat_%28back_view%29.jpg/255px-A_modern_Cricket_bat_%28back_view%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/A_modern_Cricket_bat_%28back_view%29.jpg/340px-A_modern_Cricket_bat_%28back_view%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1536" data-file-height="2048" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:A_modern_Cricket_bat_(back_view).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A modern <a href="/wiki/Sanspareils_Greenlands" title="Sanspareils Greenlands">SG</a> cricket bat (back view).</div></div></div>\n<p>Before a match begins, the team <a href="/wiki/Captain_(cricket)" title="Captain (cricket)">captains</a> (who are also players) <a href="/wiki/Toss_(cricket)" title="Toss (cricket)">toss a coin</a> to decide which team will bat first and so take the first <a href="/wiki/Innings" title="Innings">innings</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-inns_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-inns-62">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Innings" title="Innings">Innings</a> is the term used for each phase of play in the match.<sup id="cite_ref-inns_62-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-inns-62">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> In each innings, one team <a href="/wiki/Batting_(cricket)" title="Batting (cricket)">bats</a>, attempting to <a href="/wiki/Scoring_(cricket)" title="Scoring (cricket)">score</a> <a href="/wiki/Run_(cricket)" title="Run (cricket)">runs</a>, while the other team <a href="/wiki/Bowling_(cricket)" title="Bowling (cricket)">bowls</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fielding_(cricket)" title="Fielding (cricket)">fields</a> the <a href="/wiki/Cricket_ball" title="Cricket ball">ball</a>, attempting to restrict the scoring and <a href="/wiki/Dismissal_(cricket)" title="Dismissal (cricket)">dismiss</a> the batsmen.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> When the first innings ends, the teams change roles; there can be two to four innings depending upon the type of match. A match with four scheduled innings is played over three to five days; a match with two scheduled innings is usually completed in a single day.<sup id="cite_ref-inns_62-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-inns-62">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> During an innings, all eleven members of the fielding team take the field, but only two members of the batting team are on the field at any given time.<sup id="cite_ref-inns_62-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-inns-62">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> The order of batsmen is usually announced just before the match, but it can be varied.<sup id="cite_ref-Law1_57-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Law1-57">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The main objective of each team is to score more runs than their opponents but, in some forms of cricket, it is also necessary to dismiss all of the opposition batsmen in their final innings in order to win the match, which would otherwise be <a href="/wiki/Result_(cricket)#Draw" title="Result (cricket)">drawn</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-result_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-result-65">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> If the team batting last is all out having scored fewer runs than their opponents, they are said to have "lost by <i>n</i> runs" (where <i>n</i> is the difference between the aggregate number of runs scored by the teams). If the team that bats last scores enough runs to win, it is said to have "won by <i>n</i> wickets", where <i>n</i> is the number of wickets left to fall. For example, a team that passes its opponents\' total having lost six wickets (i.e., six of their batsmen have been <a href="/wiki/Dismissal_(cricket)" title="Dismissal (cricket)">dismissed</a>) have won the match "by four wickets".<sup id="cite_ref-result_65-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-result-65">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In a two-innings-a-side match, one team\'s combined first and second innings total may be less than the other side\'s first innings total. The team with the greater score is then said to have "won by an innings and <i>n</i> runs", and does not need to bat again: <i>n</i> is the difference between the two teams\' aggregate scores. If the team batting last is all out, and both sides have scored the same number of runs, then the match is a <a href="/wiki/Result_(cricket)#Tie" title="Result (cricket)">tie</a>; this result is quite rare in matches of two innings a side with only 62 happening in <a href="/wiki/First-class_cricket" title="First-class cricket">first-class matches</a> from the earliest known instance in 1741 until January 2017. In the traditional form of the game, if the time allotted for the match expires before either side can win, then the game is declared a <a href="/wiki/Result_(cricket)#Draw" title="Result (cricket)">draw</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-result_65-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-result-65">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>If the match has only a single innings per side, then a maximum number of <a href="/wiki/Over_(cricket)" title="Over (cricket)">overs</a> applies to each innings. Such a match is called a "limited overs" or "one-day" match, and the side scoring more runs wins regardless of the number of wickets lost, so that a draw cannot occur. If this kind of match is temporarily interrupted by bad weather, then a complex mathematical formula, known as the <a href="/wiki/Duckworth-Lewis_method" class="mw-redirect" title="Duckworth-Lewis method">Duckworth-Lewis method</a> after its developers, is often used to recalculate a new target score. A one-day match can also be declared a "no-result" if fewer than a previously agreed number of overs have been bowled by either team, in circumstances that make normal resumption of play impossible; for example, wet weather.<sup id="cite_ref-result_65-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-result-65">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In all forms of cricket, the umpires can abandon the match if bad light or rain makes it impossible to continue.<sup id="cite_ref-Law3_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Law3-66">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> There have been instances of entire matches, even <a href="/wiki/Test_cricket" title="Test cricket">Test matches</a> scheduled to be played over five days, being lost to bad weather without a ball being bowled: for example, the third Test of the 1970/71 series in Australia.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Bat_and_ball">Bat and ball</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Cricket_bat" title="Cricket bat">Cricket bat</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cricket_ball" title="Cricket ball">Cricket ball</a></div>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r856303569">@media all and (max-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .tmulti>.thumbinner{width:100%!important;max-width:none!important}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{float:none!important;max-width:none!important;width:100%!important;text-align:center}}</style><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:308px;max-width:308px"><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:152px;max-width:152px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:White_ball_2_(cropped).JPG" class="image"><img alt="Used white ball" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/White_ball_2_%28cropped%29.JPG/150px-White_ball_2_%28cropped%29.JPG" width="150" height="149" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/White_ball_2_%28cropped%29.JPG/225px-White_ball_2_%28cropped%29.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/White_ball_2_%28cropped%29.JPG/300px-White_ball_2_%28cropped%29.JPG 2x" data-file-width="630" data-file-height="627" /></a></div></div><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:152px;max-width:152px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Used_cricket_ball_(cropped).jpg" class="image"><img alt="Used red ball" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Used_cricket_ball_%28cropped%29.jpg/150px-Used_cricket_ball_%28cropped%29.jpg" width="150" height="150" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Used_cricket_ball_%28cropped%29.jpg/225px-Used_cricket_ball_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Used_cricket_ball_%28cropped%29.jpg/300px-Used_cricket_ball_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1110" data-file-height="1108" /></a></div></div><div style="clear:left"></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:left;background-color:transparent">Two different types of <a href="/wiki/Cricket_ball" title="Cricket ball">cricket balls</a>, both of the same size:\n<p>i) A used white ball. White balls are mainly used in <a href="/wiki/Limited_overs_cricket" title="Limited overs cricket">limited overs cricket</a>, especially in matches played at night, under <a href="/wiki/Floodlights" class="mw-redirect" title="Floodlights">floodlights</a> (left).<br />\n</p>\nii) A used red ball. Red balls are used in <a href="/wiki/Test_cricket" title="Test cricket">Test cricket</a> and <a href="/wiki/First-class_cricket" title="First-class cricket">first-class cricket</a> and some other forms of cricket (right).<br /></div></div></div>\n<p>The essence of the sport is that a <a href="/wiki/Bowling_(cricket)" title="Bowling (cricket)">bowler</a> <a href="/wiki/Delivery_(cricket)" title="Delivery (cricket)">delivers</a> (i.e., bowls) the <a href="/wiki/Cricket_ball" title="Cricket ball">ball</a> from his end of the <a href="/wiki/Cricket_pitch" title="Cricket pitch">pitch</a> towards the <a href="/wiki/Batting_(cricket)" title="Batting (cricket)">batsman</a> who, armed with a <a href="/wiki/Cricket_bat" title="Cricket bat">bat</a> is "on strike" at the other end (see next sub-section: <i>Basic gameplay</i>).\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Cricket_bat" title="Cricket bat">bat</a> is made of wood, usually <i><a href="/wiki/Salix_alba" title="Salix alba">salix alba</a></i> (white willow), and has the shape of a blade topped by a cylindrical handle. The blade must not be more than four and one quarter inches (108&#160;mm) wide and the total length of the bat not more than 38 inches (965&#160;mm). There is no standard for the weight which is usually between 2&#160;lb 7 oz and 3&#160;lb (1.1 and 1.4&#160;kg).<sup id="cite_ref-Law6_68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Law6-68">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Cricket_ball" title="Cricket ball">ball</a> is a hard leather-seamed <a href="/wiki/Spheroid" title="Spheroid">spheroid</a>, with a circumference of 22.9 centimetres (9.0&#160;in). The ball has a "seam": six rows of stitches attaching the leather shell of the ball to the string and cork interior. The seam on a new ball is prominent, and helps the bowler propel it in a less predictable manner. During matches, the quality of the ball deteriorates to a point where it is no longer usable, and during the course of this deterioration its behaviour in flight will change and can influence the outcome of the match. Players will therefore attempt to modify the ball\'s behaviour by modifying its physical properties. Polishing the ball and wetting it with sweat or saliva is legal, even when the polishing is deliberately done on one side only to increase the ball\'s <a href="/wiki/Swing_bowling" title="Swing bowling">swing through the air</a>, but the acts of rubbing other substances into the ball, scratching the surface or picking at the seam is illegal <a href="/wiki/Ball_tampering" title="Ball tampering">ball tampering</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Law5_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Law5-70">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Basic_gameplay:_bowler_to_batsman">Basic gameplay: bowler to batsman</span></h3>\n<p>During normal play, thirteen players and two <a href="/wiki/Umpire_(cricket)" title="Umpire (cricket)">umpires</a> are on the field. Two of the players are batsmen and the rest are all eleven members of the fielding team. The other nine players in the batting team are off the field in the <a href="/wiki/Cricket_pavilion" title="Cricket pavilion">pavilion</a>. The image with overlay below shows what is happening when a ball is being bowled and which of the personnel are on or close to the pitch. The photo was taken during an international match between <a href="/wiki/Australia_national_cricket_team" title="Australia national cricket team">Australia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sri_Lanka_national_cricket_team" title="Sri Lanka national cricket team">Sri Lanka</a>; <a href="/wiki/Muttiah_Muralitharan" title="Muttiah Muralitharan">Muttiah Muralitharan</a> of Sri Lanka is bowling to Australian batsman <a href="/wiki/Adam_Gilchrist" title="Adam Gilchrist">Adam Gilchrist</a>.\n</p>\n<table style="margin-left:auto;margin-right:auto;border:1px #ccc
